Now I'm getting a clearer picture:\n\n1. `ConsumerDelegate<K, V>` - An internal interface that extends `Consumer<K, V>` and provides internal methods\n2. `ClassicKafkaConsumer<K, V>` - Implements ConsumerDelegate, provides backward compatibility for the classic group protocol (pre-KIP 848)\n3. `AsyncKafkaConsumer<K, V>` - Implements ConsumerDelegate, provides the new async implementation\n\nThe key observation is that:\n- The old Kafka consumer API (`kafka.consumer.ConsumerConnector`) has been replaced\n- The new API architecture uses a `ConsumerDelegate` pattern where This provides the means by which {@link KafkaConsumer}\n * can remain the top-level facade for implementations, but allow different implementations to co-exist under\n * the covers.\n *\n * <p/>\n *\n * The current logic for the {@code ConsumerCreator} inspects the incoming configuration and determines if\n * it is using the new consumer group protocol (KIP-848) or if it should fall back to the existing, legacy group\n * protocol. This is based on the presence and value of the {@link ConsumerConfig#GROUP_PROTOCOL_CONFIG group.protocol}\n * configuration. If the value is present and equal to &quot;{@code consumer}&quot;, the {@link AsyncKafkaConsumer}\n * will be returned. Otherwise, the {@link ClassicKafkaConsumer} will be returned.\n *\n *\n * <p/>\n *\n * <em>Note</em>: this is for internal use only and is not intended for use by end users. Internal users should\n * not attempt to determine the underlying implementation to avoid coding to an unstable interface. Rather, it is\n * the {@link Consumer} API contract that should serve as the caller's interface.\n */\npublic class ConsumerDelegateCreator {\n\n    public <K, V> ConsumerDelegate<K, V> create(ConsumerConfig config,\n                                                Deserializer<K> keyDeserializer,\n                                                Deserializer<V> valueDeserializer) {\n GroupProtocol.CONSUMER)\n                return new AsyncKafkaConsumer<>(config, keyDeserializer, valueDeserializer, Optional.empty());\n            else\n                return new ClassicKafkaConsumer<>(config, keyDeserializer, valueDeserializer);\n        } catch (KafkaException e) {\n            throw e;\n        } catch (Throwable t) {\n            throw new KafkaException(\"Failed to construct Kafka consumer\", t);\n        }\n    }\n\n    public <K, V> ConsumerDelegate<K, V> create(LogContext logContext,\n Based on my research:\n\n1. **Old API**: `kafka.consumer.ConsumerConnector` (not present in current codebase - it was removed)\n\n2. **New API**: `KafkaConsumer` which delegates to:\n   - `ClassicKafkaConsumer` - for classic group protocol (pre-KIP 848)\n   - `AsyncKafkaConsumer` - for new consumer group protocol (KIP-848)\n\n3. **Key architectural changes**:\n   - Introduction of `ConsumerDelegate` pattern\n   - Use of `ConsumerDelegateCreator` factory\n   - Different internal implementations depending on group protocol\n\n4. **Key behavioral differences in offset management**:\n   - **ClassicKafkaConsumer**: Uses synchronous coordinator pattern with `ConsumerCoordinator` directly calling `coordinator.commitOffsetsSync()` and `coordinator.commitOffsetsAsync()`\n   - **AsyncKafkaConsumer**: Uses event-driven architecture with `CommitEvent`, `AsyncCommitEvent`, and event handlers\n   - Both now use `CommitRequestManager` for async implementations\n   - Offset fetching now uses `OffsetsRequestManager` instead of direct fetch\n   - Position management uses `SubscriptionState` instead of old offset storage\n\n5. **Key files to include**:\n   - KafkaConsumer.java - Main API facade\n   - Consumer.java - Interface definition\n   - ConsumerDelegate.java - Internal delegation interface\n   - ClassicKafkaConsumer.java - Classic implementation\n   - AsyncKafkaConsumer.java - Async implementation\n   - ConsumerDelegateCreator.java - Factory pattern\n   - CommitRequestManager.java - Offset commit management\n   - sophisticated internal architecture change in apache/kafka. While the old ConsumerConnector interface is no longer present in the current codebase (it was removed in favor of the newer API), the current implementation demonstrates a thoughtful migration strategy using a delegation pattern.\\n\\nThe new API is centered around KafkaConsumer (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/KafkaConsumer.java), which implements the Consumer interface (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/Consumer.java). However, the actual implementation is delegated to one of two internal implementations through the ConsumerDelegateCreator factory (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ConsumerDelegateCreator.java):\\n\\n1. ClassicKafkaConsumer (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ClassicKafkaConsumer.java) - Provides backward compatibility with the classic group protocol (pre-KIP-848). This implementation uses synchronous coordination patterns where offset commits are handled through ConsumerCoordinator with methods like coordinator.commitOffsetsSync() for synchronous commits and coordinator.commitOffsetsAsync() for asynchronous commits.\\n\\n2. AsyncKafkaConsumer (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/AsyncKafkaConsumer.java) - Implements the new consumer group protocol (KIP-848) using an event-driven architecture. Instead of direct coordinator calls, it uses ApplicationEventHandler to queue AsyncCommitEvent and SyncCommitEvent objects that are processed asynchronously by background threads.\\n\\nKEY BEHAVIORAL DIFFERENCES IN OFFSET MANAGEMENT:\\n\\n(1) Synchronous vs. Event-Driven Architecture: \\n- ClassicKafkaConsumer uses direct method calls: commitSync() calls coordinator.commitOffsetsSync() directly and blocks until completion.\\n- AsyncKafkaConsumer uses event queuing: commitSync() creates a CompletableFuture and enqueues a SyncCommitEvent to be processed by background threads, then waits for the future to complete.\\n\\n(2) Offset Commit Request Handling:\\n- Both implementations now delegate commit operations to CommitRequestManager (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/CommitRequestManager.java), which manages the actual OffsetCommit protocol requests to the broker.\\n- ClassicKafkaConsumer uses this through ConsumerCoordinator which internally uses CommitRequestManager.\\n- AsyncKafkaConsumer uses CommitRequestManager directly through its event-driven background thread.\\n\\n(3) Offset Fetching and Position Management:\\n- Both use OffsetsRequestManager (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/OffsetsRequestManager.java) for managing ListOffset requests to retrieve offsets from brokers.\\n- Both use OffsetFetcher (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/OffsetFetcher.java) as a utility for offset fetching operations.\\n- Both use SubscriptionState (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/SubscriptionState.java) to track partition assignments and current fetch positions.\\n\\n(4) Callback Handling:\\n- ClassicKafkaConsumer immediately invokes offset commit callbacks within the application thread.\\n- AsyncKafkaConsumer uses OffsetCommitCallbackInvoker to queue callbacks for execution, providing better isolation between user code and the consumer.\\n\\n(5) Configuration Strategy:\\n- The choice between implementations is controlled by the group.protocol configuration setting.\\n- Setting group.protocol=\\\"consumer\\\" activates AsyncKafkaConsumer (new protocol).\\n- Setting group.protocol=\\\"classic\\\" (or not setting it) uses ClassicKafkaConsumer for backward compatibility.\\n\\nThe ConsumerDelegate interface (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ConsumerDelegate.java) enables this pluggable architecture, extending the Consumer interface with internal methods for testing and framework use.\\n\\nIn Apache Camel (components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/KafkaConsumer.java), the migration is transparent - Camel's KafkaConsumer wraps the Apache Kafka Consumer API and automatically benefits from whichever implementation (Classic or Async) is selected based on the configuration.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":1910,"cache_creation_input_tokens":3664,"cache_read_input_tokens":57884,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":3664},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"7198bcb7-c4f6-4103-aeac-5da61964f9e1","uuid":"1858a9f2-04ba-4123-82ad-ef13a2df2950"}

While the old ConsumerConnector interface is no longer present in the current codebase (it was removed in favor of the newer API), the current implementation demonstrates a thoughtful migration strategy using a delegation pattern.\\n\\nThe new API is centered around KafkaConsumer (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/KafkaConsumer.java), which implements the Consumer interface (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/Consumer.java). However, the actual implementation is delegated to one of two internal implementations through the ConsumerDelegateCreator factory (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ConsumerDelegateCreator.java):\\n\\n1. ClassicKafkaConsumer (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ClassicKafkaConsumer.java) - Provides backward compatibility with the classic group protocol (pre-KIP-848). This implementation uses synchronous coordination patterns where offset commits are handled through ConsumerCoordinator with methods like coordinator.commitOffsetsSync() for synchronous commits and coordinator.commitOffsetsAsync() for asynchronous commits.\\n\\n2. AsyncKafkaConsumer (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/AsyncKafkaConsumer.java) - Implements the new consumer group protocol (KIP-848) using an event-driven architecture. Instead of direct coordinator calls, it uses ApplicationEventHandler to queue AsyncCommitEvent and SyncCommitEvent objects that are processed asynchronously by background threads.\\n\\nKEY BEHAVIORAL DIFFERENCES IN OFFSET MANAGEMENT:\\n\\n(1) Synchronous vs. Event-Driven Architecture: \\n- ClassicKafkaConsumer uses direct method calls: commitSync() calls coordinator.commitOffsetsSync() directly and blocks until completion.\\n- AsyncKafkaConsumer uses event queuing: commitSync() creates a CompletableFuture and enqueues a SyncCommitEvent to be processed by background threads, then waits for the future to complete.\\n\\n(2) Offset Commit Request Handling:\\n- Both implementations now delegate commit operations to CommitRequestManager (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/CommitRequestManager.java), which manages the actual OffsetCommit protocol requests to the broker.\\n- ClassicKafkaConsumer uses this through ConsumerCoordinator which internally uses CommitRequestManager.\\n- AsyncKafkaConsumer uses CommitRequestManager directly through its event-driven background thread.\\n\\n(3) Offset Fetching and Position Management:\\n- Both use OffsetsRequestManager (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/OffsetsRequestManager.java) for managing ListOffset requests to retrieve offsets from brokers.\\n- Both use OffsetFetcher (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/OffsetFetcher.java) as a utility for offset fetching operations.\\n- Both use SubscriptionState (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/SubscriptionState.java) to track partition assignments and current fetch positions.\\n\\n(4) Callback Handling:\\n- ClassicKafkaConsumer immediately invokes offset commit callbacks within the application thread.\\n- AsyncKafkaConsumer uses OffsetCommitCallbackInvoker to queue callbacks for execution, providing better isolation between user code and the consumer.\\n\\n(5) Configuration Strategy:\\n- The choice between implementations is controlled by the group.protocol configuration setting.\\n- Setting group.protocol=\\\"consumer\\\" activates AsyncKafkaConsumer (new protocol).\\n- Setting group.protocol=\\\"classic\\\" (or not setting it) uses ClassicKafkaConsumer for backward compatibility.\\n\\nThe ConsumerDelegate interface (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ConsumerDelegate.java) enables this pluggable architecture, extending the Consumer interface with internal methods for testing and framework use.\\n\\nIn Apache Camel (components/camel-kafka/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/component/kafka/KafkaConsumer.java), the migration is transparent - Camel's KafkaConsumer wraps the Apache Kafka Consumer API and automatically benefits from whichever implementation (Classic or Async) is selected based on the configuration.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
